A Tit-for-Tat style strategy — starting cooperative and then mirroring the opponent's previous move — is well-known to be highly effective in iterated prisoner's dilemma tournaments. By cooperating first, I give the opponent a chance to establish a mutually beneficial pattern. If they defect, I can adjust accordingly in future rounds.

Additionally, since this is a tournament with 11 players and my history is visible to all, cooperating in round 1 helps build a reputation that may encourage other agents to cooperate with me in future games, maximizing my long-term cumulative score across the entire tournament.

                        LLM PROMPT TEMPLATE REFERENCE

Below is the prompt structure sent to LLM agents during the game:

[System Prompt Template]
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
You are agent '{agent_id}', playing a multi-round decision-making game with another player.
In each round, you and the other player must independently choose either 'cooperate' or 'defect'.
There is no communication other than seeing each other's choice history.

--- Payout Matrix ---
- You choose 'cooperate', Opponent chooses 'cooperate': You get R, Opponent gets R
- You choose 'defect', Opponent chooses 'defect': You get P, Opponent gets P
- You choose 'cooperate', Opponent chooses 'defect': You get S, Opponent gets T
- You choose 'defect', Opponent chooses 'cooperate': You get T, Opponent gets S

--- Goal ---
Maximize your own cumulative score across all rounds. Think strategically about how your choices impact future rounds.
[Optional: Custom Profile/Directives text defined in system_prompt]
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[User Prompt Template]
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Current Round: {round_num}

--- Game History So Far ---
Round 1: You chose '{my_choice}', Opponent chose '{opponent_choice}'. Your payoff: X, Opponent payoff: Y.
Round 2: ...

Submit your choice for the current round ('cooperate' or 'defect').
